   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Dental, alveolar and postalveolar trills
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Alveolar_trill&amp;redirect=no" title="Alveolar trill">
       Alveolar trill
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       "r (IPA)" redirects here. For the 'r' sound (as in English
       <b>
        r
       </b>
       ed) often transcribed
       <i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /r/
        </span>
       </i>
       for convenience, see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_approximant" title="Alveolar approximant">
        Alveolar approximant (
        <i>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ɹ]
         </span>
        </i>
        )
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        alveolar trill
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound, used in many spoken
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
        dental
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
        alveolar
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
        postalveolar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">
        trills
       </a>
       is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        r
       </span>
       ⟩, and the equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        r
       </code>
       . It is commonly called the
       <b>
        rolled R
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        rolling R
       </b>
       , or
       <b>
        trilled R
       </b>
       . Quite often, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        r
       </span>
       ⟩ is used in phonemic transcriptions (especially those found in dictionaries) of languages like
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       that have
       <a href="/wiki/Rhotic_consonant" title="Rhotic consonant">
        rhotic consonants
       </a>
       that are not an alveolar trill. That is partly for ease of typesetting and partly because ⟨r⟩ is the letter used in the orthographies of such languages.
      </p>
      <p>
       In most
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European languages
       </a>
       , the sound is at least occasionally
       <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">
        allophonic
       </a>
       with an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_tap" title="Alveolar tap">
        alveolar tap
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɾ]
       </span>
       , particularly in unstressed positions. Exceptions include
       <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">
        Albanian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_Greek" title="Cypriot Greek">
        Cypriot Greek
       </a>
       , and a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">
        Armenian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       dialects, which treat them as distinct phonemes.
      </p>
      <p>
       People with
       <a href="/wiki/Ankyloglossia" title="Ankyloglossia">
        ankyloglossia
       </a>
       may find it exceptionally difficult to articulate the sound because of the limited mobility of their tongues.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voiced_alveolar_trill">
        Voiced alveolar trill
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_trills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Voiced alveolar trill">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 16em;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background: #f2f2ce;">

          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>

         </a>

      <p>
       Most commonly, the alveolar trill is voiced.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_trills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Features of the alveolar trill:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">
         trill
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing air over the articulator so that it vibrates.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
         dental
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
         alveolar
        </a>
        or
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-alveolar_consonant" title="Post-alveolar consonant">
         post-alveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated behind upper front teeth, at the
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
         alveolar ridge
        </a>
        or behind the alveolar ridge. It is most often
        <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
         apical
        </a>
        , which means that it is pronounced with the tip of the tongue.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

          s
         </i>

         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_tap" title="Voiced alveolar tap">

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voiced_alveolar_fricative_trill">
        <span id="Voiced_alveolar_fricative_trill">
         Voiced alveolar fricative trill
        </span>
        <span id="Raised_alveolar_non-sonorant_trill">
        </span>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_trills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Voiced alveolar fricative trill">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 16em;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background: #f2f2ce;">
         Raised alveolar trill
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           r̝
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPA_number" title="IPA number">
          IPA number
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         122 429
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         Encoding
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
          X-SAMPA
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <code>
          r_r
         </code>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         Listen
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <div class="mediaContainer" style="width:150px">
            <audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="2.2247619047619" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Raised_alveolar_non-sonorant_trill.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_3" preload="none" style="width:150px">
             <source data-bandwidth="109732" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (110 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c7/Raised_alveolar_non-sonorant_trill.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/>
             <source data-bandwidth="136912" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/c7/Raised_alveolar_non-sonorant_trill.ogg/Raised_alveolar_non-sonorant_trill.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/>
            </audio>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div style="text-align:center">
          <small>
           <a href="/wiki/File:Raised_alveolar_non-sonorant_trill.ogg" title="File:Raised alveolar non-sonorant trill.ogg">
            source
           </a>
           <span style="font-weight:bold;">
            ·
           </span>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
            help
           </a>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">
        Czech
       </a>
       , there are two contrasting alveolar trills. Besides the typical apical trill, written
       <i>
        r
       </i>
       , there is another, laminal trill, written
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/%C5%98" title="Ř">
         ř
        </a>
       </i>
       , in words such as
       <i>
        rybá
        <b>
         ř
        </b>
        i
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈrɪbaːr̝ɪ]
       </span>
       'fishermen' and the common surname
       <i>
        Dvo
        <b>
         ř
        </b>
        ák
       </i>
       . Its manner of articulation is similar to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [r]
       </span>
       but is
       <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
        laminal
       </a>
       and the body of the tongue is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raised_(phonetics)" title="Raised (phonetics)">
        raised
       </a>
       . It is thus partially
       <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
        fricative
       </a>
       , with the frication sounding rather like
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʒ]
       </span>
       but not so retracted. It sounds like a simultaneous
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [r]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʒ]
       </span>
       , and non-native speakers may pronounce it as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [rʐ]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [rʒ]
       </span>
       . In the IPA, it is typically written as ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        r
       </span>
       ⟩ plus the raising diacritic, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        r̝
       </span>
       ⟩, but it has also been written as laminal ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        r̻
       </span>
       ⟩.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (Before the 1989
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPA_Kiel_Convention" title="IPA Kiel Convention">
        IPA Kiel Convention
       </a>
       , it had a dedicated symbol ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɼ
       </span>
       ⟩.) The
       <a href="/wiki/Kobon_language" title="Kobon language">
        Kobon language
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">
        Papua New Guinea
       </a>
       also has a fricative trill, but the degree of frication is variable.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features_2">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_trills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Features of the voiced alveolar fricative trill:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is fricative trill, which means it is a non-sibilant fricative and a trill pronounced simultaneously.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
         laminal
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
         alveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the blade of the tongue at the
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
         alveolar ridge
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">
        Examples
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">
          Czech
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dankovičová_32-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Dankovičová-32">
           [32]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOWLCZ_33-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-SOWLCZ-33">
           [33]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
          <a href="#cite_note-34">
           [34]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SiPoCh_35-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-SiPoCh-35">
           [35]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="cs">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czech_alphabet" title="Czech alphabet">
            čty
            <b>
             ř
            </b>
            i
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">
           <span class="fn">
            <span style="white-space:nowrap">
             <a href="/wiki/File:Cs-%C4%8Dty%C5%99i.ogg" title="About this sound">
              <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
             </a>
            </span>
            <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Cs-%C4%8Dty%C5%99i.ogg" title="Cs-čtyři.ogg">
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              [ˈt͡ʃtɪr̝ɪ]
             </span>
            </a>
           </span>
           <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
            (
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              help
             </span>
            </a>
            ·
            <a href="/wiki/File:Cs-%C4%8Dty%C5%99i.ogg" title="File:Cs-čtyři.ogg">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              info
             </span>
            </a>
            )
           </small>
          </span>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'four'
        </td>
        <td>
         May be a
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_fricative#Voiced_alveolar_non-sibilant_fricative" title="Voiced alveolar fricative">
          non-sibilant fricative
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOWLCZ_33-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-SOWLCZ-33">
           [33]
          </a>
         </sup>
         It contrasts with
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /r/
         </span>
         and
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʒ/
         </span>
         . See
         <a href="/wiki/Czech_phonology" title="Czech phonology">
          Czech phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Kashubian_language" title="Kashubian language">
          Kashubian
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treder_36-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-treder-36">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AUDIENCE" title="Wikipedia:AUDIENCE">
            <span title="Wikipedia:AUDIENCE">
             example needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         Only some northern and northwestern speakers.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treder_36-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-treder-36">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Kobon_language" title="Kobon language">
          Kobon
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AUDIENCE" title="Wikipedia:AUDIENCE">
            <span title="Wikipedia:AUDIENCE">
             example needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         Amount of frication variable. May also be a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap#Voiced_alveolar_raised_non-sonorant_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
          fricative flap
         </a>
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">
          Polish
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Some dialects
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="pl">
           <a href="/wiki/Polish_alphabet" title="Polish alphabet">
            <b>
             rz
            </b>
            eka
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">
           <span class="fn">
            <span style="white-space:nowrap">
             <a href="/wiki/File:Cs-%C5%99eka.ogg" title="About this sound">
              <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
             </a>
            </span>
            <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/45/Cs-%C5%99eka.ogg" title="Cs-řeka.ogg">
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              [ˈr̝ɛkä]
             </span>
            </a>
           </span>
           <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
            (
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              help
             </span>
            </a>
            ·
            <a href="/wiki/File:Cs-%C5%99eka.ogg" title="File:Cs-řeka.ogg">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              info
             </span>
            </a>
            )
           </small>
          </span>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'river'
        </td>
        <td>
         Contrasts with
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /r/
         </span>
         and
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʐ/
         </span>
         . Present in areas from
         <a href="/wiki/Starogard_Gda%C5%84ski" title="Starogard Gdański">
          Starogard Gdański
         </a>
         to
         <a href="/wiki/Malbork" title="Malbork">
          Malbork
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         and those south, west and northwest of them,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         area from
         <a href="/wiki/Lubawa" title="Lubawa">
          Lubawa
         </a>
         to
         <a href="/wiki/Olsztyn" title="Olsztyn">
          Olsztyn
         </a>
         to
         <a href="/wiki/Olecko" title="Olecko">
          Olecko
         </a>
         to
         <a href="/wiki/Dzia%C5%82dowo" title="Działdowo">
          Działdowo
         </a>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-3">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         south and east from
         <a href="/wiki/Wiele%C5%84" title="Wieleń">
          Wieleń
         </a>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-4">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         around
         <a href="/wiki/Wo%C5%82omin" title="Wołomin">
          Wołomin
         </a>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-5">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         southeast from
         <a href="/wiki/Ostr%C3%B3w_Mazowiecka" title="Ostrów Mazowiecka">
          Ostrów Mazowiecka
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-6">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         and west from
         <a href="/wiki/Siedlce" title="Siedlce">
          Siedlce
         </a>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-7">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         from
         <a href="/wiki/Brzeg" title="Brzeg">
          Brzeg
         </a>
         to
         <a href="/wiki/Opole" title="Opole">
          Opole
         </a>
         and those north of them,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-8">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         and roughly from
         <a href="/wiki/Racib%C3%B3rz" title="Racibórz">
          Racibórz
         </a>
         to
         <a href="/wiki/Nowy_Targ" title="Nowy Targ">
          Nowy Targ
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-9">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Most speakers, as well as standard Polish merge it with
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʐ/
         </span>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-10">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         and speakers maintaining the distinction (which is mostly the elderly) sporadically do that too.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-11">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Polish_phonology" title="Polish phonology">
          Polish phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
          Portuguese
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr157_38-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-gr157-38">
           [38]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="pt">
           <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">
            o
            <b>
             s r
            </b>
            ins
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [u ˈr̝ĩʃ]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'the kidneys'
        </td>
        <td>
         Possible realization of the sequence
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /sr/
         </span>
         for speakers who realize
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /r/
         </span>
         as
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [r]
         </span>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr157_38-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-gr157-38">
           [38]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_phonology" title="Portuguese phonology">
          Portuguese phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Silesian_language" title="Silesian language">
          Silesian
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Gmina_Istebna" title="Gmina Istebna">
          Gmina Istebna
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dąbrowska_39-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Dąbrowska-39">
           [39]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="szl">
           um
           <b>
            rz
           </b>
           ił
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ˈumr̝iw]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         '(he) died'
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         Contrasts with
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /r/
         </span>
         and
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʒ/
         </span>
         . Merges with
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʐ/
         </span>
         in most Polish dialects.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Jablunkov" title="Jablunkov">
          Jablunkov
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dąbrowska_39-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-Dąbrowska-39">
           [39]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [

        <td>

        <td>

       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">
          Slovak
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Northern dialects
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-12">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>
         </sup>

          <span lang="sk">
           <a href="/wiki/Slovak_orthography" title="Slovak orthography">
            <b>
             ř
            </b>
            yka
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ˈr̝ɪkä]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'river'
        </td>
        <td>
         Only in a few dialects near the Polish border.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frykatywner_37-13">
          <a href="#cite_note-frykatywner-37">
           [37]
          </a>

                       </div>
                       <p>
                        Where symbols appear in pairs, the leftmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" title="Voiceless consonant">
                         voiceless consonant
                        </a>
                        , and the rightmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" title="Voiced consonant">
                         voiced consonant
                        </a>
                        .
                       </p>
                       <p>
                        Shaded areas denote articulations judged to be impossible.
